=100  \\$4Editor$aPage, Christopher$d1952-$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3675871$915727
=100  \\$4Composer$aHildegard of Bingen$915728
=245  \\$aAbbess Hildegard of bingen (1098-1179): sequences and hymns
=260  \\$aNewton Abbot$bAntico edition
=300  \\$a27
=520  \\$aThis edition contains all the pieces by Hildegard which are labelled Sequentia in the two manuscript sources of her songs, together with O viridissima virga which should, perhaps, be classed as a sequence and Ave,generosa, one of Hildegard's finest hymns. Twelfth century sequences generally consisted of verses comprising a pair of versicles, each versicle being set to the same melody and the melody being different for each verse, producing a melodic form AA BB CC and so on. Contains: Columba aspexit Ave, generosa O ignis spiritus O lerusalem,aurea civitas O Euchari O viridissima virga O presul vere civitatis O Ecclesia O virga ac diadema Text of songs are included in both the notes and in poetic form in back.

=020  \\$a9780226133669
=041  \\$ae
=100  \\$aD'Accone, Frank A.$d1931-2022$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q17579937$916520
=245  \\$aThe civic muse: music and musicians in Siena during the middle ages and the renaissance
=260  \\$aChicago & London$bThe University of Chicago Press$c1997
=300  \\$a862
=520  \\$aSiena, blessed with neither the aristocratic nor the ecclesiastical patronage enjoyed by music in other northern Italian centers like Florence, nevertheless attracted first-rate composers and performers from all over Europe. As Frank A. DAccone shows in this scrupulously documented study, policies developed by the town to favor the common good formed the basis of Sienas ambitious musical programs. 

Based on decades of research in the towns archives, DAccones The Civic Muse brilliantly illuminates both the sacred and the secular aspects of more than three centuries of music and music-making in Siena. After detailing the history of music and liturgy at Sienas famous cathedral and of civic music at the Palazzo Pubblico, DAccone describes the crucial role that music played in the daily life of the town, from public festivities for foreign dignitaries to private musical instruction. Putting Siena squarely on the Renaissance musical map, DAccones monumental study will interest both musicologists and historians of the Italian Renaissance.

=245  \\$aFive Anglo-Norman motets
=260  \\$aNewton Abbot$bAntico edition
=300  \\$a15
=520  \\$aHere are collected all the surviving motets in Anglo-Norman, the form of French spoken by the aristocracy in thirteenth-century England. Only one, Volez oyer le castoy, is an Anglo-Norman original; the others, Duce creature, Veine pleine de duur, Amor vient tout and Au queer ay un maus, are adaptations of French or Latin motets. For three solo singers, but also performable instrumentally. vi + 11 pages.

=245  \\$aFive ballades for the house of Foix
=260  \\$bAntico edition$c1988
=300  \\$a22
=520  \\$aFour of these ballades (Phiton Phiton, Le mont Aon, Se Galaas and Se July Cesar) honour Gaston Febus, the hero of the motets in AE23. The other piece Se Alixandre praises Gastons nephew and successor Mathieu de Foix. Se Galaas and Se July Cesar are in the rhythmically complex mannered style fashionable in the later fourteenth century. Probably intended for entirely vocal performance, these works also sound well on instruments. ix + 22 pages.

=041  \\$afre$dlat
=100  \\$aRoesner, Edward H.$4edt$916579
=245  \\$aLe Magnus Liber Organi de Notre-Dame de Paris
=260  \\$aMonaco$bÉditions de l'Oiseau-Lyre$c1993
=300  \\$a4 vols. (xcix-358+xci-332+?+? pages)
=520  \\$aMAGNUS LIBER ORGANI
Parisian Liturgical Polyphony from the 12th and 13th Centuries
7 volumes
General Editor: Edward H. Roesner
The Magnus Liber Organi was composed for the cathedral of Notre Dame, Paris, during the brilliant cultural Renaissance of the twelfth century and the first decades of the thirteenth century. The work of Leoninus and other musicians, it may be considered as the greatest single achievement in the development of early polyphony. The revision and renotation of the Great Book by Perotinus and his contemporaries were equally important; the creation of the three- and four-voice organa (the earliest known examples of music for more than two voices) is one of the most extraordinary moments in the development of Western polyphony. This new edition, undertaken by an international team of scholars working under Professor Edward H. Roesner, will present the Parisian liber organi in all its richness and diversity for the first time in a complete modern edition. Subscription to the series is open to individuals as well as institutions; each volume is also available separately.

=245  \\$aSongs of the trouvères
=260  \\$aNewton Abbot$bAntico edition
=300  \\$a28
=520  \\$aThis anthology of nineteen trouvere songs dating from the twelfth and thirteenth centuries includes six works by Gace Brul as well as songs by eight other named poet-composers and three anonymous pieces; the choice illustrates virtually the full range of trouvre song. All the compositions are monophonic and may be found useful by instrumentalists as well as singers. The music has been recorded by Gothic Voices as The Spirits of England and France, Volume II (Hyperion, CDA66773). xxiii + 28 pages.

=245  \\$aThe sounding object
=260  \\$bMondo Estremo Publishing$c2003
=300  \\$a399 pages
=520  \\$aDuring the last couple of decades we have been involved in a revolution: computer-based virtual, distributed, and augmented realities increasingly affect our perception of the world. Despite the abundant technological facilities, we are now faced with lack of knowledge on how to generate sounds which please a perceptual and cognitive system whose evolution developed slowly, over many thousands of years. The authors of this book are striving to find and develop principles that may open the way to get appropriate informative sounds out of future artifacts. They present novel research in perception, physics, numeral analysis, computer science, and human-machine interaction.

=100  \\$4aut$aDel Mar, Jonathan$916215
=245  \\$aComplete Sonatas for Pianoforte:$bCritical Commentary
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aKassel$bBärenreiter$c2020

=490  \\$aBärenreiter Urtext
=505  \\$gSigns and conventions -- Appendices -- Critical Commentary -- Sonatas in E-flat major, F minor, D major WoO 47 -- Sonatas in F minor, A major, C major op. 2 -- Sonata in E-flat major op. 7 -- Sonatas in C minor, F major, D major op. 10 -- Sonata in C minor op . 13 (Pathétique) -- Sonatas in E major, G major op. 14 -- Sonata in B-flat major op. 22 -- Sonata in A-flat major op. 26 -- Sonatas in E-flat major, C-sharp minor op. 27 -- Sonata in D major op. 28 -- Sonatas in G major, D minor, E-flat major op. 31 -- Sonatas in G minor, G major op. 49 -- Sonata in C major op. 53 -- Sonata in F major op. 54 -- Sonata in F minor op. 57 -- Sonata in F-sharp major op. 78 -- Sonata in G major op. 79 -- Sonata in E-flat major op. 81a (Lebewohl, Abwesenheit und Wiedersehn) -- Sonata in E minor op . 90 -- Sonata in A major op. 101 -- Sonata in B-flat major op. 106 -- Sonata in E major op. 109 -- Sonata in A-flat major op. 110 -- Sonata in C minor op . 111 -- Appendix 1: Suspected errors -- Appendix 2: Alternative readings -- Appendix 3: First movement: Differences between A1 and A2 -- Appendix 4: Authentic readings in later sources -- Bibliography
=520  \\$aAlongside the Urtext edition of Beethoven’s 35 piano sonatas which sets new standards for the 21st century, world-renowned Beethoven expert Jonathan Del Mar presents a Critical Commentary to this body of works.

With diligence and factual accuracy, he documents readings and editorial decisions, discusses problematic sections and provides answers for questions that have occupied and divided scholars for decades, including Beethoven’s notational idiosyncrasies and particular issues relating to performance practice. The Critical Commentary is more than a mere list of findings: It is a fascinating read offering valuable glimpses into Beethoven’s compositional process. This scholarly contribution is unparalleled in its precision and indispensable for in-depth studies of Beethoven’s piano sonatas.

=100  \\$aHérold, Ferdinand$d1791-1833$4cmp$921075
=245  \\$aOuverture de Missolonghi
=300  \\$a[8-8 pages]$bpamphlet stitch binding
=500  \\$aRefering to the siege of Missolonghi by the Turks during the Greek War of Independence (1821-1829).
=500  \\$aIncidental Music
=500  \\$aFerdinand Hérold wrote the overture, chorus and other pieces for the heroic drama “The Last Day of Messolonghi” (Le Dernier Jour de Missolonghi, drame héroïque en trois actes, en vers, avec des chants - edited by Barba Paris, 1828) also called "le Siège de Missolonghi" or  the mélodrame « Le dernier jour de Missolonghi » . This drame héroïque en vers, Le Dernier Jour de Missolonghi  written by Jean Georges Ozaneaux (1795-1852) was created april10th 1828 at the Odéon in Paris. Its ouverture has remained thanks to a delicious motif that has become popular. 
=500  \\$a"Hérold avait écrit une très-belle ouverture, qui a figuré longtemps au programme des concerts, des airs de chant et de danse délicieux, et une prière d'un beau caractère." (B. Jouvin, Hérold. Sa Vie, ses Oeuvres, Paris, 1868, p.151)
